{"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_013wJZASZ6z1337Hu1VnbTop","type":"tool_result","content":"   100→// directionality is complicated to manage in a transactionless system, but\n   101→// without it we can't ensure sane behavior in the face of different forms of\n   102→// trouble. For example, a rogue HA controller instance could end up racing\n   103→// and making multiple bindings that are indistinguishable, resulting in\n   104→// potential data loss.\n   105→//\n   106→// This controller is designed to work in active-passive high availability\n   107→// mode. It *could* work also in active-active HA mode, all the object\n   108→// transitions are designed to cope with this, however performance could be\n   109→// lower as these two active controllers will step on each other toes\n   110→// frequently.\n   111→//\n   112→// This controller supports pre-bound (by the creator) objects in both\n   113→// directions: a PVC that wants a specific PV or a PV that is reserved for a\n   114→// specific PVC.\n   115→//\n   116→// The binding is two-step process. PV.Spec.ClaimRef is modified first and\n   117→// PVC.Spec.VolumeName second. At any point of this transaction, the PV or PVC\n   118→// can be modified by user or other controller or completely deleted. Also,\n   119→// two (or more) controllers may try to bind different volumes to different\n   120→// claims at the same time. The controller must recover from any conflicts\n   121→// that may arise from these conditions.\n   122→\n   123→// Number of retries when we create a PV object for a provisioned volume.\n   124→const createProvisionedPVRetryCount = 5\n   125→\n   126→// Interval between retries when we create a PV object for a provisioned volume.\n   127→const createProvisionedPVInterval = 10 * time.Second\n   128→\n   129→// CSINameTranslator can get the CSI Driver name based on the in-tree plugin name\n   130→type CSINameTranslator interface {\n   131→\tGetCSINameFromInTreeName(pluginName string) (string, error)\n   132→}\n   133→\n   134→// CSIMigratedPluginManager keeps track of CSI migration status of a plugin\n   135→type CSIMigratedPluginManager interface {\n   136→\tIsMigrationEnabledForPlugin(pluginName string) bool\n   137→}\n   138→\n   139→// PersistentVolumeController is a controller that synchronizes\n   140→// PersistentVolumeClaims and PersistentVolumes. It starts two\n   141→// cache.Controllers that watch PersistentVolume and PersistentVolumeClaim\n   142→// changes.\n   143→type PersistentVolumeController struct {\n   144→\tvolumeLister       corelisters.PersistentVolumeLister\n   145→\tvolumeListerSynced cache.InformerSynced\n   146→\tclaimLister        corelisters.PersistentVolumeClaimLister\n   147→\tclaimListerSynced  cache.InformerSynced\n   148→\tclassLister        storagelisters.StorageClassLister\n   149→\tclassListerSynced  cache.InformerSynced\n   150→\tpodLister          corelisters.PodLister\n   151→\tpodListerSynced    cache.InformerSynced\n   152→\tpodIndexer         cache.Indexer\n   153→\tNodeLister         corelisters.NodeLister\n   154→\tNodeListerSynced   cache.InformerSynced\n   155→\n   156→\tkubeClient                clientset.Interface\n   157→\teventBroadcaster          record.EventBroadcaster\n   158→\teventRecorder             record.EventRecorder\n   159→\tvolumePluginMgr           vol.VolumePluginMgr\n   160→\tenableDynamicProvisioning bool\n   161→\tresyncPeriod              time.Duration\n   162→\n   163→\t// Cache of the last known version of volumes and claims. This cache is\n   164→\t// thread safe as long as the volumes/claims there are not modified, they\n   165→\t// must be cloned before any modification. These caches get updated both by\n   166→\t// \"xxx added/updated/deleted\" events from etcd and by the controller when\n   167→\t// it saves newer version to etcd.\n   168→\t// Why local cache: binding a volume to a claim generates 4 events, roughly\n   169→\t// in this order (depends on goroutine ordering):\n   170→\t// - volume.Spec update\n   171→\t// - volume.Status update\n   172→\t// - claim.Spec update\n   173→\t// - claim.Status update\n   174→\t// With these caches, the controller can check that it has already saved\n   175→\t// volume.Status and claim.Spec+Status and does not need to do anything\n   176→\t// when e.g. volume.Spec update event arrives before all the other events.\n   177→\t// Without this cache, it would see the old version of volume.Status and\n   178→\t// claim in the informers (it has not been updated from API server events\n   179→\t// yet) and it would try to fix these objects to be bound together.\n   180→\t// Any write to API server would fail with version conflict - these objects\n   181→\t// have been already written.\n   182→\tvolumes persistentVolumeOrderedIndex\n   183→\tclaims  cache.Store\n   184→\n   185→\t// Work queues of claims and volumes to process. Every queue should have\n   186→\t// exactly one worker thread, especially syncClaim() is not reentrant.\n   187→\t// Two syncClaims could bind two different claims to the same volume or one\n   188→\t// claim to two volumes. For example, a rogue HA controller instance could end up racing\n// and making multiple bindings that are indistinguishable, resulting in\n// potential data loss.\n//\n// This controller is designed to work in active-passive high availability\n// mode. It *could* work also in active-active HA mode, all the object\n// transitions are designed to cope with this, however performance could be\n// lower as these two active controllers will step on each other toes\n// frequently.\n//\n// This controller supports pre-bound (by the creator) objects in both\n// directions: a PVC that wants a specific PV or a PV that is reserved for a\n// specific PVC.\n//\n// The binding is two-step process. PV.Spec.ClaimRef is modified first and\n// PVC.Spec.VolumeName second. At any point of this transaction, the PV or PVC\n// can be modified by user or other controller or completely deleted. Also,\n// two (or more) controllers may try to bind different volumes to different\n// claims at the same time. This cache is\n\t// thread safe as long as the volumes/claims there are not modified, they\n\t// must be cloned before any modification. These caches get updated both by\n\t// \"xxx added/updated/deleted\" events from etcd and by the controller when\n\t// it saves newer version to etcd.\n\t// Why local cache: binding a volume to a claim generates 4 events, roughly\n\t// in this order (depends on goroutine ordering):\n\t// - volume.Spec update\n\t// - volume.Status update\n\t// - claim.Spec update\n\t// - claim.Status update\n\t// With these caches, the controller can check that it has already saved\n\t// volume.Status and claim.Spec+Status and does not need to do anything\n\t// when e.g. volume.Spec update event arrives before all the other events.\n\t// Without this cache, it would see the old version of volume.Status and\n\t// claim in the informers (it has not been updated from API server events\n\t// yet) and it would try to fix these objects to be bound together.\n\t// Any write to API server would fail with version conflict - these objects\n\t// have been already written.\n\tvolumes persistentVolumeOrderedIndex\n\tclaims  cache.Store\n\n\t// Work queues of claims and volumes to process. interconnected components that handle CSI volume operations across the cluster.\\n\\n**CSI Driver Plugin (pkg/volume/csi/)**: The core CSI integration is implemented in the CSI plugin at pkg/volume/csi/csi_plugin.go. This plugin registers itself via ProbeVolumePlugins() and implements the volume.VolumePlugin interface. The csiPlugin struct manages CSI driver registration through the RegistrationHandler, which validates and registers CSI drivers when their sockets are detected by the kubelet's plugin watcher. The plugin maintains references to CSI driver listers and volume attachment listers.\\n\\n**CSI Node Plugin Client (pkg/volume/csi/csi_client.go)**: The csiClient interface defines the contract for communicating with CSI node plugins via gRPC. The csiDriverClient implementation provides methods like NodeGetInfo, NodePublishVolume, NodeUnpublishVolume, NodeStageVolume, and NodeUnstageVolume that correspond to CSI node service RPC operations. These methods enable volume mounting, unmounting, and staging operations on nodes. The client also supports capabilities like NodeExpandVolume for inline expansion and NodeGetVolumeStats for volume metrics.\\n\\n**Volume Mounter (pkg/volume/csi/csi_mounter.go)**: The csiMountMgr struct implements the volume.Mounter interface and coordinates mounting operations. It uses the CSI client to perform NodePublishVolume and NodeStageVolume operations, managing volume paths and metadata throughout the mount lifecycle.\\n\\n**Volume Attacher/Detacher (pkg/volume/csi/csi_attacher.go)**: The csiAttacher struct implements both volume.Attacher and volume.Detacher interfaces. It handles volume attachment by creating VolumeAttachment objects in the API server and waiting for the external attacher sidecar to complete the attachment. The Attach method creates a VolumeAttachment resource and polls for attachment status, while Detach removes attachments and verifies detachment completion.\\n\\n**Block Volume Support (pkg/volume/csi/csi_block.go)**: Provides block device volume mapping and unmapping support for CSI drivers.\\n\\n**Volume Expansion (pkg/volume/csi/expander.go)**: Handles CSI volume expansion operations through NodeExpandVolume RPC calls.\\n\\n**CSI Node Info Manager (pkg/volume/csi/nodeinfomanager/nodeinfomanager.go)**: Manages CSI node information by creating and updating CSINode objects that advertise driver capabilities, accessible topologies, and node IDs to the control plane.\\n\\n**Attach/Detach Controller (pkg/controller/volume/attachdetach/)**: This controller manages the lifecycle of volume attachments cluster-wide. The main controller in attach_detach_controller.go orchestrates attachment and detachment operations. The reconciler (reconciler/reconciler.go) runs a periodic loop that compares desired vs actual state of world and triggers attachment/detachment operations. The controller uses DesiredStateOfWorld to track which volumes should be attached to which nodes (populated by desired_state_of_world_populator.go based on pod specifications) and ActualStateOfWorld to track the current attachment state. The statusupdater/node_status_updater.go updates node status with attachment information.\\n\\n**PersistentVolume Controller (pkg/controller/volume/persistentvolume/pv_controller.go)**: This controller bridges CSI operations to the core storage API. It synchronizes PersistentVolumes and PersistentVolumeClaims, implementing dynamic provisioning through the provisionClaim method. When a PVC with a StorageClass is created, the controller calls findProvisionablePlugin to locate the appropriate provisioner (either in-tree or external). For CSI-based provisioning, it calls provisionClaimOperationExternal which invokes the external provisioner sidecar. The controller also manages volume binding, reclamation, and deletion. It tracks operation timestamps for metrics and handles CSI migration by detecting when in-tree plugins have migrated to CSI.\\n\\n**Volume Expansion Controller (pkg/controller/volume/expand/expand_controller.go)**: Deprecated controller that adds necessary annotations for external volume expansion. It detects when volumes need expansion and communicates this to external expansion components.\\n\\n**CSI Storage Resources (pkg/registry/storage/)**: Registry implementations for CSI-related API objects - CSIDriver, CSINode, and CSIStorageCapacity provide storage backends in the API server. VolumeAttachment objects persist attachment state between the controller and external attacher/detacher sidecars.\\n\\nThe complete flow: When a pod is created requiring a CSI volume, the PVC controller provisions the volume via external provisioner. The attach/detach controller detects the volume need and orchestrates attachment through VolumeAttachment objects. The kubelet's CSI plugin mounts the volume using the CSI node client. External sidecars (attacher, provisioner, resizer) watch these API objects and perform actual storage operations.\"\n}\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":13,"cache_creation_input_tokens":2688,"cache_read_input_tokens":59423,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":2688},"output_tokens":1,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"7fe05643-451a-43e5-be7d-ad0b06fb3338","uuid":"402360ef-f899-4f52-ad55-73d4761c8db7"}

interconnected components that handle CSI volume operations across the cluster.\\n\\n**CSI Driver Plugin (pkg/volume/csi/)**: The core CSI integration is implemented in the CSI plugin at pkg/volume/csi/csi_plugin.go. This plugin registers itself via ProbeVolumePlugins() and implements the volume.VolumePlugin interface. The csiPlugin struct manages CSI driver registration through the RegistrationHandler, which validates and registers CSI drivers when their sockets are detected by the kubelet's plugin watcher. The plugin maintains references to CSI driver listers and volume attachment listers.\\n\\n**CSI Node Plugin Client (pkg/volume/csi/csi_client.go)**: The csiClient interface defines the contract for communicating with CSI node plugins via gRPC. The csiDriverClient implementation provides methods like NodeGetInfo, NodePublishVolume, NodeUnpublishVolume, NodeStageVolume, and NodeUnstageVolume that correspond to CSI node service RPC operations. These methods enable volume mounting, unmounting, and staging operations on nodes. The client also supports capabilities like NodeExpandVolume for inline expansion and NodeGetVolumeStats for volume metrics.\\n\\n**Volume Mounter (pkg/volume/csi/csi_mounter.go)**: The csiMountMgr struct implements the volume.Mounter interface and coordinates mounting operations. It uses the CSI client to perform NodePublishVolume and NodeStageVolume operations, managing volume paths and metadata throughout the mount lifecycle.\\n\\n**Volume Attacher/Detacher (pkg/volume/csi/csi_attacher.go)**: The csiAttacher struct implements both volume.Attacher and volume.Detacher interfaces. It handles volume attachment by creating VolumeAttachment objects in the API server and waiting for the external attacher sidecar to complete the attachment. The Attach method creates a VolumeAttachment resource and polls for attachment status, while Detach removes attachments and verifies detachment completion.\\n\\n**Block Volume Support (pkg/volume/csi/csi_block.go)**: Provides block device volume mapping and unmapping support for CSI drivers.\\n\\n**Volume Expansion (pkg/volume/csi/expander.go)**: Handles CSI volume expansion operations through NodeExpandVolume RPC calls.\\n\\n**CSI Node Info Manager (pkg/volume/csi/nodeinfomanager/nodeinfomanager.go)**: Manages CSI node information by creating and updating CSINode objects that advertise driver capabilities, accessible topologies, and node IDs to the control plane.\\n\\n**Attach/Detach Controller (pkg/controller/volume/attachdetach/)**: This controller manages the lifecycle of volume attachments cluster-wide. The main controller in attach_detach_controller.go orchestrates attachment and detachment operations. The reconciler (reconciler/reconciler.go) runs a periodic loop that compares desired vs actual state of world and triggers attachment/detachment operations. The controller uses DesiredStateOfWorld to track which volumes should be attached to which nodes (populated by desired_state_of_world_populator.go based on pod specifications) and ActualStateOfWorld to track the current attachment state. The statusupdater/node_status_updater.go updates node status with attachment information.\\n\\n**PersistentVolume Controller (pkg/controller/volume/persistentvolume/pv_controller.go)**: This controller bridges CSI operations to the core storage API. It synchronizes PersistentVolumes and PersistentVolumeClaims, implementing dynamic provisioning through the provisionClaim method. When a PVC with a StorageClass is created, the controller calls findProvisionablePlugin to locate the appropriate provisioner (either in-tree or external). For CSI-based provisioning, it calls provisionClaimOperationExternal which invokes the external provisioner sidecar. The controller also manages volume binding, reclamation, and deletion. It tracks operation timestamps for metrics and handles CSI migration by detecting when in-tree plugins have migrated to CSI.\\n\\n**Volume Expansion Controller (pkg/controller/volume/expand/expand_controller.go)**: Deprecated controller that adds necessary annotations for external volume expansion. It detects when volumes need expansion and communicates this to external expansion components.\\n\\n**CSI Storage Resources (pkg/registry/storage/)**: Registry implementations for CSI-related API objects - CSIDriver, CSINode, and CSIStorageCapacity provide storage backends in the API server. VolumeAttachment objects persist attachment state between the controller and external attacher/detacher sidecars.\\n\\nThe complete flow: When a pod is created requiring a CSI volume, the PVC controller provisions the volume via external provisioner. The attach/detach controller detects the volume need and orchestrates attachment through VolumeAttachment objects. The kubelet's CSI plugin mounts the volume using the CSI node client. External sidecars (attacher, provisioner, resizer) watch these API objects and perform actual storage operations.\"\n}\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}
